<Time>1393642249154< /Time><text>Great dimsum place with lots of seating and tables for large parties. Call ahead on the weekend to check how long the wait is, especially because sometimes they let you put your name on the waiting list.  They haven't been strict about having all members of our party present before seating, though I have heard this can vary with the hostess.  If you're craving a different jook than the one being pushed around in the cart, you can still order it from the connected cafe.  I love their jook with sliced fish.

Despite the long wait and curt servers, when it comes to dim sum basics Joy Luck delivers.  My favorites are cheung fun (rice noodle roll with shrimp), siu mai, fried taro dumpling, lo-bak-go turnip cake, steamed spare ribs, and black sesame ball dessert.

Service is absolutely and consistently terrible, as expected with many Chinese restaurants, but the dimsum is worth it.  The dinner selection is great too, lots of traditional chinese dishes.  My favorites are the flavorful lobster E-Fu noodles and steamed rock cod.< /text></record>

< review>
Lovely play structure for my kids.

What a beautiful designed and architected landscape.

As a long time resident of Marin County, and now raising children here, I have seen a bit of run down happening to some of the places I have been to over the 20+years I have loved here, but these many structures are beginning to be rebuilt or renovated.

Hopefully this playground will get a small make over soon.

Overall though, Marin is a much more beautiful place to live and raise your children than say, San Francisco and the rest of the Bay Area.

We are so lucky to have so many options like Millenium Park so our kids don't get bored of the usual down the street park or our backyard.<//review>

<Text>This is usually a good playground to take young children to. They have a tot side of the park that bigger kids are not encouraged to play in and so that does help keep the little ones safer from being run over and such. Normally I would have rated this park higher but on this occasion when we visited, the kids were having to avoid a hornet's nest which had built up in one of the towers of the play structure. While I'm sure it will be removed soon, at this time, in September of 2018, it was a bit of a nuisance. Aside from that, a great place for kids to play including a large grass field right next to the play structures where they can run around or play ball as well. There is a usable bathroom facility and also a usable water fountain. I say usable because both of them are in slight disrepair but still functional. All in all a good spot to burn off some of the kids' energy.</Text><Pics>None</Pics>< Response>

Indoor dining tonight 3/26/2021. This a Japanese owned ramen restaurant. I had their black garlic tonkotsu ramen $15, geso (squid) fry $7, red rice beer $5, yuki white peach $5. Having ate over hundreds of bowls of ramen throughout my years in Japan, I can tell their ramen is authentic. The flavors are fantastic and when I closed my eyes, it brought back memories of when I ate at ramen parlors in Tokyo. This place is better though as I was the only person dining indoors. There's no rush feeling you get when there's a line outside waiting. Here are the reasons why I absolutely love their ramen:

- Âë≥‰ªò„ÅëÁéâÂ≠ê ramen egg soft boiled and is marinated. Perfect jelly on the inside
- broth is heavy and have been cooked for hours
- great garlic flavor
- perfectly soft chashu
- fresh noodles

<Time>1513823886221</Time><rate>4<//rate>< Text>
The best Tonkotsu ramen in JTown by far. Broth is rich and creamy. Wonderful on a cold, winter day in The City. Reasonably priced for what you get. Love their warm, gooey smoked egg in the hot broth. Pressing your own fresh garlic cloves is a novel idea. Never had that experience before. You do have to ask for a garlic press though. The best deal on the menu is to order the Kakuni Don instead of the Small Bites size for your table to share - you get Waraku's heavenly tasting braised pork belly, but also rice and more gooey egg. Also enjoyed their hot black tea, different from the usual watery green tea you get a Japanese restaurant these days. Service was ok, nothing memorable or outstanding (hence the 4 stars).</Text>

<date>1492101830743< /date><Review>It was already 9pm and we wanted to eat some ramen~ We ended up in japantown after trying to go to another ramen shop and seeing a huge line... decided we didn't have the time and headed here because there are many many ramen places here. The only one we knew was already closed so we came to waraku because of the food reviews and because it was still pretty to, good sign, i thought.

We got the tonkotsu ramen ($10.99) with extra noodles on the side ($2), and a mini kakuni rice bowl ($4). The bowls look smaller than the regular one, But the quality is good, and I think quantity is enough too. There just probably won't be many leftovers to bring home. The ramen came with an egg, some thin pieces of meat, a mushroom type, ginger.. and the broth was less salty than average, which was good~~
The rice bowl had just 1 piece of meat, But it was a very big piece. The meat was very tasty, also sweet, and the rice was impregnated with the sauce, very yummy. Btw we ordered all without spring onions, but othrewise you'd have that too.
Service was quite attentive, some of the servers are Japanese and some others are not , But they're certainly trained to look japanese.

<review>I was rather disappointed by Waraku. From the rather bland decor to unenthusiastic service to lackluster ramen.

I had their tsukemen, which is supposed to be a much heavier, richer broth than standard tonkatsu. Unfortunately, that wasn‚Äôt the case at Waraku where the tsukemen was thin, and with exception of a heap of scallions, relatively light on flavor. Noodles were a bit unusual, coming with some kind of oil and seasoning on them. Temperature is a huge part of ramen, and Waraku fell short there, too, serving the tsukemen broth too hot which prevents it from sticking to the noodles, and serving an overcooked ajitama egg at refrigerated temperatures.

Drink options left much to be desired. There weren‚Äôt many great pairings with the food, and even the sake menu seemed content to put middling options on a pedestal.

One positive note: the chicken karaage, while far from traditional, was really delicious. I ordered the plate with rice, but I think the wait staff misheard me and I wound up with the protein-heavy version sans rice, but no complaints.<//review>< Response>

<review>I had the spicy tonkotsu ramen, tako wasabi, and some karage at Waraku. The tako wasabi was pretty straightforward and good; plenty of wasabi and prepared well.
The karage came with a lemon wedge and some mayo based sauce to dip in. The seasoning was pretty light, but the breading was very crispy. Enjoyed it very much.
The ramen was decently spicy, noodles were pretty straightforward, not made in house. The broth was a bit light on flavor, which was slightly masked by the spicyness. They add cilantro to some of the ramen, which is a little odd, but not bad. The ajitamago (seasoned boiled egg) was well seasoned, but a bit more well done than I prefer. Overall, I enjoyed it. Not quite as good as Yamadaya or Marufuku, but nowhere near the wait time, sometimes convenience trumps all.</review><pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN8IXxQdMTrxmTknxO4Nbu-kXpnF7oj9paznkPD=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pictures>< Resp>

<text>My youngest son turned me on to Waraku.
Told me it was "different" from our regular "ramen joint". We were first in at opening. The young lady that served us was very soft spoken so it was a lil difficult to understand her but her friendliness and level of "cuteness" made up for that.
Now listen... this is "different".
Their ramen is made with a "bone broth" that I imagine is cultivated the same as sourdough bread (Google the process)
It was DELICIOUS!
So delicious that I went in strictly as a spectator as my son was hungry and I was not...
I tasted his ramen (this is very telling as he is not one to share but it was so good and different from the norm that he WANTED me to taste it)...
I tasted his ramen and was so turned on by the bone broth flavor, I ordered one for myself purely for flavor and not for hunger.
Here's where it gets tricky...
One of the great challenges for any restaurant is consistency.
I failed to mention the ramen has a roasted garlic component. On My sons dish... it was PERFECT!
I guess they rushed mine as the garlic was just over the burn line. Instead of roasted, my garlic was burned. As much as I tried to muscle thru it as I didn't want a refire and really wanted to have the bone broth win the flavor battle... the burned garlic won. Shoulda sent it back. Ate half and took it home.
A lil water and soy sauce fixed it right up!
Meanwhile, their "MACHA FLAN (?)"?!
THA BOMB!!üò≤. NOT TOO "MACHAY" DIDN'T TASE LIKE I WAS EATING GRASS WHICH WAS MY FEAR WHEN I ORDERED IT. really, it rocked. Overall, something special here at WARAKU!!
Definitely going to give them a second try and would suggest it to anyone that asked.
That's why I took the time for this. That and hopefully the owners/cooks see this and balance the garlic roast a lil better cause if it wasn't for the overpowering effect of the burnt garlic... this would 5+ stars!
Give WARAKU a try.
Enjoy!

<userid>103392898122416277360</userid><user_name>Geoff Watson<//user_name><date>1461114338061< /date><rate>3</rate>< Text>
Waraku used to be my absolute favorite ramen place in the city.  But lately I have been finding their fare inconsistent at best.  Don't get me wrong, it is still better than most.  The smoked eggs have come out practically hard boiled the last few times, rather than the runny yolk that everybody wants.  They also seem to be very affected by how busy they are.  Best case, go here on a "school night" when restaurants are supposed to be slow.  The broth will be much better than average, the noodles with that great QQ taste, and if you happen in on a good night, 3/4 of the meat will be great.  If it's a Friday or Saturday night, save yourself the time and go get a burrito or something.</Text>

We decided to try the new ramen restaurant.

The noodle broth was cooked for more than 12 hours. It has a lot of rich flavors. The noodle was done right, not too soggy. Priced reasonably which is similar to other restaurants in Japantown.

I also love the sashimi salad. It's a big bowl of yummy salad and fresh fish. So worth it for less than $10 I think.

I'm excited about the new ramen place in the neighborhood.< /text>

< Text>
The usual disclaimer when it comes to Japanese food: I'm super picky. I can't say Waraku had really awesome ramen, but there was one surprise element that warranted a 4-star review.

I got the tonkotsu broth ramen (there are only 3 choices). The broth was decent, but not as thick as it should be. The noodles were average, nothing to rave about there. Chashu, good, not amazing.

What made this meal so awesome? THE PORK BELLY. Definitely get that. You'll wish you got two orders of it.</Text>

Walked in and signed up on waiting list. The list clearly states their non-forgiving policy. However, other groups who signed up after us were seated before us (our entire party was there).

All of this and they were NOT extremely busy.< /Text>

<rating>5<//rating>< review>
Well y'all.
I've found my favorite ramen in the Bay (for now).

The ramen is AMAZE but their other food items were also all REALLY good which I didn't expect of a ramen-specific place.

Worth the wait (if there is one). Get the tonkotsu ramen, $9 - the broth is rich and borderline creamy, even. The mouthfeel and taste is a must-try and the noodles are perfect. Comes with fresh garlic - ask for a garlic press!

We also tried:
Sashimi salad - which is HUGE for $9 and totally a steal
Tako (octopus) wasabi & ika shio kara (salted squid), $3 each - portion was small but so fresh -- interesting and concentrated flavors
Agedashi tofu $5 - HOLY - yes plz
Takoyaki $4.5 - ON POINT

DEFINITELY RETURNING AND RECOMMENDING.
Oh yes, the interior is beautiful and upscale. But I'm hurr to eat.<//review>

<Gmap_id>0x808580bed8e90009:0x4bfcacfeba03db0c< /Gmap_id><pics>None</pics>< Text>
I came here for lunch with my girlfriend and cousin and ordered the Deluxe Tonkotsu Ramen. This ramen place is probably my favorite in San Francisco right now because of all the ingredients they put into the ramen, the service, and the decorations in the restaurant. The noodles were delicious and had a nice chew to them. The broth was very flavorful and rich. We also asked for garlic and they gave us a garlic press.I liked how you could press your own fresh garlic cloves. The chashu was tender but the pork belly wasn't as good as the chashu. I liked that this ramen came with corn because my girlfriend's favorite food is corn and probably made this place one of our favorites. The egg was runny just the way I like it but everyone else at my table had an overcooked egg. Sucks for them =P. I'll probably come back often to eat the Deluxe Tonkotsu Ramen.< /Text>

<Time>1384974037365</Time><userid>101745605215871584532< /userid>< Text>
Came here for lunch during the J-pop festival. It was a really nice and well decorated place. Service was good and fast.

I had the deluxe tonkotsu ramen with the spicy miso paste (not spicy at all). The broth was very savory and flavorful. The pork was soft and tender. The EGG had tons of flavor which was a good surprise. Overall pretttttttttttty good ramen. I'd give it 4 stars but I feel they messed up on one of the key components - the noodles. My noodles were under cooked and were too chewy for my liking. The portions were also too small for the price. 13$ and I was hungry 10 minutes after eating. I feel like noodles are cheap, just throw a bunch in there to fill us up.

I'd come back again to give it another shot, especially cause there aren't too many great ramen places in the city (or have yet to find).

Must haves:
THAT EGG<//Text>

< Text>
Was so sad to see the former restaurant this space hosted, Bushi-Tei, no longer there, but was happily surprised to have a high quality Ramen noodle spot instead! Love the decor, very soothing and relaxing, they kept much of the same ambiance as before (minus the large communal table), and the service is prompt and friendly. The focus is ramen, so if you don't like ramen noodles, you might not find much else to satisfy your hunger here, however it does offer some other interesting appetizers and side dishes. I always prefer the Shoyu (chicken-based broth) Ramen, and the Gyoza appetizer has yet to disappoint!</Text>
